## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: constitutive modeling / thermomechanical materials science
**Analysis**: The task seeks the stress-strain-temperature relationship (constitutive law) for a material. Stress typically increases with strain via hardening and decreases with temperature via thermal softening, often modeled as separable multiplicative contributions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (linear elastic): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime, small strains)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for plastic strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type (no strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - (c2 * T)**c3) (power-law hardening with homologous temperature softening)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear softening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(-c2 * T) (thermally activated softening)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power law to avoid singularity at zero strain)
- Swift with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (combined Swift hardening and Arrhenius softening)
- Polynomial constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T + c3 * epsilon * T (quadratic with cross-term)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse form: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (softening at large strains)
- Multiplicative separable: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law in both strain and temperature)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * exp(-c2 * T) (saturating hardening with exponential thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening behavior → Power-law epsilon**c or saturating form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)); concavity indicates hardening type
- Thermal softening as multiplicative factor → Stress often factorizes as f(epsilon) * g(T), where g(T) is a decreasing function of T
- Linear thermal softening → (1 - c*T) or (T_melt - T) terms common for moderate temperature ranges
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation → exp(-c/T) or exp(-c*T) appears when thermally activated dislocation mechanisms dominate
- Strain-temperature coupling → Cross terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicate that hardening rate itself depends on temperature
- Yield stress offset → Additive constant c0 represents initial yield stress before hardening begins (Ludwik-type)
- Saturation stress at large strains → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicates dislocation density saturation
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature enters as (T/T_ref) raised to a power, reflecting normalized thermal effects
